<Review>Let me say AVOID this place.

I asked the lady for brown rice, she gives me white then says I still have to pay for it. Okay no big deal. Next I ask for two entree's of chicken. She makes sure to find the smallest, most burnt pieces she can possibly find, then cuts them down and puts them back! Came out to $8 for what equated to and tasted like beef jerky. On top of that everything was COLD. Will never come back. I say if you're looking for something quick and tasty Chinese type, just drive a few minutes up the road to Panda Express. They will at least feed you. Do not give these people your business.

<Text>Shameful what bad management and ill-trained staff can do to such a beautiful YMCA.

I grew going to the YMCA. I learned how to swim and play tennis at the Magdalena YMCA in Encinitas as child. Always had great experiences and made me think very highly of the YMCA.

No doubt, this is a great facility in terms of amenities and features, but if those amenities aren't maintained, then was it worth the investment?

Compared to other YMCA's, the big noticeable difference with this location is the general upkeep of the Locker Room. I can't speak about the Women's locker room, but the Men's locker room is not well maintained and generally in poor condition. Looking back, in other locations I recall always seeing the cleaning staff coming in and out of the locker rooms. In all my visits here, I do not recall ever seeing an attendant inside the locker rooms.

In general, they have a good selection of group exercise classes and a good schedule. My wife and I did several classes and enjoyed most of them. The only classes I often found lacking inspiration were the Spin classes. So if you are thinking of joining for that, I wouldn't recommend it.

It's a great facility, but not very large. The weight area is a bit tight and it can get pretty crowded. I found myself doing free weights in the outside workout space to avoid the crowds. Not the best option if its cold or too hot.

What finally made me cancel my membership was that my locker was broken into and everything was stolen. The fact that it happened wasn't why I cancelled, but how it was handled is why I cancelled. My locker was pried opened and the initial statements from the staff member were the following:
- "Are you sure that was your locker" : while looking at a broken empty locker*
- "Yeah, this has happened a couple of times in the past few weeks" : So you know it's happening and nothing is done to prevent it?
- "Well there's nothing we can do": Why even have cameras at all? Why check badges? I'm sure people taking there families there want a sense of security.

In my conversation over the phone, the Director offered nothing more than canned and scripted answers. No empathy (Even if its fake!), no solutions and no assurances. They didn't bother looking at the cameras. They just said the police had to do. SD Police in City Heights has bigger things to worry about then locker room theft. I filed a police report, but of course, nothing was done.

For those wondering...Within 30 minutes of me finding my locker broken into, I had almost $1,000 dollars in charges on my debit and credit cards from nearby places like GameStop, Bob's smoke shop and Vons. Whoever is breaking into the lockers, obviously knows what they are doing and they know the YMCA is a soft target.< /Text><time>1534532562662<//time>< user_id>

< Review>
Dr Wu is such an incredibly caring and nice orthodontist. He at first told us to come back when my 7-year-old son was older, but when his teeth started coming in sideways because of severe crowding, he told us right away we were ready to go ahead and do Damon braces. Damon braces create space for teeth right at the root, instead of having to use medieval palette expanders. I think the teeth end up looking more natural/befitting of your face that way, also. I met with many other orthodontists, and Dr. Wu was the most honest, had the most integrity, and used the most modern technology. He was so unbelievably nice and patient with us: we had to go in all the time, even on weekends, because my very young son would mess around with things in his mouth, and he never once made us feel bad or charged us extra. Rather, he reassured us that it wasn't my son's fault, that these things happen with young kids. He got his braces off after a year and a half and now has room for the rest of his teeth to come in, so we'll see if we ever need Phase 2. Thank you, Dr. Wu and all your lovely staff for my son's happy, healthy smile!</Review>

I am a busy Stanford grad student who came to see Dr. Wu to treat a pretty severe overbite (over 10mm).  I was skeptical initially that he would be able to correct my problem without any type of jaw surgery or tooth extractions and with my busy schedule I did not want to deal with those options.  Invisalign was not an option for me so he placed Damon Braces along with a device with little metal springs on the sides to help realign my lower jaw to treat me overbite. <Text>The team seems good natured and helped me with my issue (replace broken spoke, tune wheel). People wore masks and more or less seemed to be practicing responsible social distancing/behavior (most of the work is done outside).

It took a bit longer than I was expecting and with nowhere to sit, be prepared to stand around outside for a while (2 hours in my case). I would recommend asking up front how long things will take and see if you can give them your number and/or come back later assuming you didn't ride your bike there.  Crew is friendly and will likely chat with you if you're into in that.

Once they finished with my bike and let me test it out to my satisfaction, they jumped straight to their next job so I sat around for a few minutes waiting for someone to ring me up. After another 10 minutes of waiting I asked again about getting rung up and they charged me $40. Again, probably ended up waiting longer because I wasn't pressing them constantly for a bill.

I was originally quoted $30-35 for the wheel, I recall $10 for treating the chain (which I think was just a spray of WD-40). They said they didn't charge me tax so I don't know exactly what the billing scheme was. I brought in my own parts for replacement and let them have the leftovers since they probably have more use for spokes than I do.

After ringing me up, the owner basically stood over me until I posted a review here on Google Reviews.  I think their work is fine, crew is friendly, but I think I'll check out other bike shops in the area before coming back to this one.<//Text>< Name>

<user_name>Sam Kang</user_name><Time>1602444143714</Time><Rating>5<//Rating>< Review>
The young guy who works here is a really good bike mechanic.

Brought my bike in here to fix a flat.  20 bucks and did it in 20 minutes with no wait.   Then wanted to lube the gears and tighten the brakes.  Extra 40 bucks for all of that.   Kind of pricey but I rarely get work on my bike done so agreed.

Once everything was done I rode the bike home then realized 1st gear to 2nd wasn't shifting and vice versa.

Brought it right back and I said the gears were having a problem shifting from 2nd to 1st.   It's not like they weren't working before.   But now they weren't shifting at all whatsoever.

Young dude steps in, tests the bike and agreed the gears weren't shifting.  Did some work with a screwdriver and a wrench.   5 minutes later, the gears were shifting again.

Hey as long as the shop gets the job done, I can't complain.</Review>
